### [1] [Not Truly Multilingual: Script Consistency as a Missing Dimension in VLM Evaluation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17188)
*Prabhjot Singh,Bhushan Pawar,Madhu Reddiboina,Rajvee Sheth*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: PuMVR reveals script-level gaps in multilingual VLMs across Punjabi scripts; proposes Script Consistency Rate (SCR) as a metric for script-agnostic evaluation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To address the assumption of one-to-one language-orthography mapping in multilingual VLM benchmarks and reveal under-explored script diversity in languages with multiple scripts.

Method: Create PuMVR benchmark with 1,000 parallel image-text instances across Punjabi's three scripts (Gurmukhi, Shahmukhi, Roman). Evaluate 10 state-of-the-art VLMs using cross-script and cross-script-in-context tests. Use McNemar tests to analyze script-pair differences. Propose SCR as a metric.

Result: Found substantial Script Gap: models perform differently across scripts with accuracy deltas up to 16%. Visual input boosts performance but does not close the orthographic gap. Cross-script transfer is brittle, indicating script-locked representations. SCR can drop to 24.8% on the benchmark.

Conclusion: Current so-called multilingual VLMs are not truly multi-script. SCR should be used for script-agnostic evaluation to ensure equitable access; data and code are released for reproducibility.

Abstract: Current multilingual evaluations for Vision-Language Models (VLMs) assume a one-to-one mapping between language and orthography, overlooking billions of users of multi-script languages. We introduce PuMVR (Punjabi Multimodal Visual Reasoning), a benchmark of 1,000 strictly parallel image-text instances across Punjabi's three active scripts: Gurmukhi, Shahmukhi, and Roman. Evaluating 10 state-of-the-art VLMs, we expose a substantial and systematic Script Gap. Models frequently solve visual tasks in one script while failing identical tasks in another, with accuracy deltas reaching 16%. Crucially, visual input boosts absolute performance uniformly yet does not close the orthographic gap. Furthermore, cross-script in-context transfer is highly brittle, exposing script-locked knowledge representation. Supported by McNemar tests across all script pairs, our findings demonstrate that current "multilingual" VLMs are not truly multi-script. We propose the Script Consistency Rate (SCR), which falls as low as 24.8% on our benchmark, as a mandatory metric for script-agnostic evaluation to ensure equitable AI access. Data and code are available at: https://github.com/prabhjotschugh/Not-Truly-Multilingual-PuMVR.

</details>


### [2] [Quantum Enchanced Multi-Scale CNN with Bi-directional Mamba for Crop Field Analysis](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17222)
*Mohammad Salman Khan,Ehsan Atoofian,Saad B. Ahmed*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: BiSpectral Mamba integrates multi-scale CNN, spectral attention, bidirectional state-space modeling, and quantum-inspired learning for HSI crop classification, achieving 84.83% OA on UAVHSI-Crop.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Address high spectral dimensionality, spatial complexity, class imbalance, and limited labeled samples in hyperspectral image (HSI) classification; leverage combined spatial-spectral representations and sequential modeling to improve robustness.

Method: 1) Multi-scale CNN backbone for hierarchical spatial-spectral feature extraction with multi-resolution fusion; 2) spectral attention to emphasize informative bands; 3) BiSpectral Mamba module modeling long-range dependencies in forward and backward directions by treating hyperspectral feature maps as sequential tokens; 4) class-weighted optimization and feature fusion to mitigate imbalance and stabilize training; 5) potential integration of quantum-inspired learning.

Result: On UAVHSI-Crop, the framework achieves an overall accuracy of 84.83%, demonstrating that the combination of convolutional, attention-based, and state-space modeling components yields robust spatial-spectral feature learning for crop classification and generalizes to broader agricultural remote sensing tasks.

Conclusion: The proposed BiSpectral Mamba framework advances HSI crop classification by fusing multi-scale CNNs, spectral attention, and bidirectional state-space representations, with demonstrated effectiveness on UAVHSI-Crop and potential applicability to crop disease detection, yield prediction, and soil moisture estimation. It highlights the promise of structured state-space and quantum-inspired architectures for hyperspectral analysis; future work could include ablations, cross-dataset validation, and real-time deployment considerations.

Abstract: Hyperspectral image (HSI) crop analysis is essential for precision agriculture because it captures rich spectral and spatial information for accurate crop monitoring and assessment. However, HSI classification remains challenging due to high spectral dimensionality, spatial complexity, class imbalance, and limited labeled samples. To address these challenges, this paper proposes a BiSpectral Mamba-based framework that combines multi-scale convolutional feature extraction, spectral attention, bidirectional state-space modeling, and quantum-inspired learning. A multi-scale CNN backbone first extracts hierarchical spatial-spectral representations through feature fusion across multiple resolutions. A spectral attention mechanism then emphasizes informative bands while suppressing redundant and noisy channels. The refined features are processed by a BiSpectral Mamba module that captures long-range dependencies in both forward and backward directions by modeling hyperspectral feature maps as sequential tokens. In addition, class-weighted optimization and feature fusion strategies are incorporated to improve training stability and mitigate class imbalance. Experimental evaluation on the UAVHSI-Crop dataset demonstrates the effectiveness of the proposed framework, achieving an overall accuracy of 84.83%. The results show that integrating convolutional, attention-based, and state-space modeling components enables robust spatial-spectral feature learning for crop classification. The proposed framework also shows potential for broader agricultural and remote sensing applications, including crop disease detection, yield prediction, and soil moisture estimation, while highlighting the effectiveness of structured state-space and quantum-inspired architectures for hyperspectral image analysis.

</details>


### [3] [Beyond Benchmarks: Continuous Edge Inference for Fine-Grained Roadside Perception](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17241)
*Aditya Mishra,Haroon Lone*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Edge-TSR demonstrates deployment-aware, continuous edge inference on resource-constrained hardware (Jetson Orin Nano), revealing that static-image benchmarks overstate real-world streaming performance; it introduces track-aware temporal stabilization that improves consistency and accuracy while sustaining real-time operation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Benchmark-centric evaluations inadequately capture deployment realities for streaming edge AI, including temporal instability, thermal throttling, and workload-driven variability; there is a need for deployment-oriented evaluation and stabilization techniques.

Method: Proposes Edge-TSR, a system integrating detection, tracking, fine-grained classification, and a lightweight track-aware temporal stabilization mechanism. Evaluated on NVIDIA Jetson Orin Nano during a long-duration vehicular deployment (55 minutes, 26 km route) to characterize inference quality, latency, throughput, and thermal behavior; releases a sample annotated streaming-video evaluation dataset and full system implementation.

Result: Found consistent 20–30% relative degradation when moving from static-image evaluation to real-world streaming across three state-of-the-art baselines. Edge-TSR recovers up to 10.16% classification accuracy over per-frame baselines while maintaining real-time performance (16.18 FPS) and safe thermal limits on a single embedded device without cloud offload.

Conclusion: Deployment-aware evaluation and temporal inference stabilization are necessary for robust, continuously operating edge AI systems in real-world sensing deployments; Edge-TSR demonstrates viability and provides resources to support reproducible deployment-centric evaluation.

Abstract: Continuous AI inference on resource-constrained edge hardware introduces deployment effects that are largely invisible to conventional benchmark evaluation, including temporal instability in streaming video, thermal throttling under sustained load, and workload-dependent performance variability. We present Edge-TSR, a deployment-oriented continuous edge inference system for sustained roadside perception on the NVIDIA Jetson Orin Nano. Edge-TSR integrates detection, tracking, fine-grained classification, and a lightweight track-aware temporal stabilization mechanism that improves streaming inference consistency with negligible computational overhead. Our central finding is that benchmark-centric evaluation systematically overstates deployed edge inference performance. Across three state-of-the-art baselines, we observe consistent 20-30% relative degradation when transitioning from static-image evaluation to real-world streaming deployment. Edge-TSR addresses this gap through temporal inference stabilization, recovering up to 10.16% classification accuracy over per-frame inference baselines while maintaining sustained real-time performance under continuous operation. We evaluate the complete system under diverse real-world deployment conditions, jointly characterizing inference quality, latency, throughput, and thermal behavior during long-duration operation. A 55-minute vehicular deployment over a 26 km route demonstrates sustained operation at 16.18 FPS within safe thermal limits on a single embedded device without cloud offload. Our findings show that deployment-aware evaluation and temporal inference stabilization are necessary components of continuously operating edge AI systems intended for real-world sensing deployments. We release a sample annotated streaming video evaluation dataset and full system implementation to support reproducible deployment-centric evaluation.

</details>


### [4] [Landsat-Sentinel-2 Algal Bloom Mapping Using Vision Transformers: Model Description, Implementation, and Examples](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17242)
*Thainara Lima,Vitor Martins*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Vision Transformer-based coastal algal bloom mapping at 30 m resolution from Landsat-Sentinel-2, outperforming spectral indices under cloud/glint conditions and enabling fragmented bloom detection.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Global, high-resolution, consistent coastal bloom monitoring is hampered by limited spectral coverage and non-harmonized products; deep learning offers a data-driven avenue to leverage multi-sensor, high-resolution data.

Method: Compared four transformer-based architectures against a CNN baseline on a globally distributed dataset of bloom patches; evaluated across optical water types and atmospheric/surface conditions; assessed under cloud/glint stress in time series; compared with MODIS products.

Result: All DL models detect floating blooms with omission/commission errors in the 8–65% range; Swin Transformer best under cloud/glint; spectral indices generate many false positives; higher spatial resolution improves detection of fragmented blooms.

Conclusion: Deep learning, particularly vision transformers, is a reliable tool for medium-resolution, consistent monitoring of floating algal blooms in dynamic coastal environments, enabling detection of fragmented and irregular blooms that coarse sensors miss.

Abstract: Coastal algal bloom monitoring requires frequent, spatially detailed, and globally consistent observations, provided by Landsat-8/9 and Sentinel-2 A/B/C. Together, these missions offer over a decade of medium-resolution multispectral imagery with near-global coverage every 2-3 days, enabling the detection of fragmented bloom structures not resolvable by coarse ocean-color sensors. However, their use in aquatic environments remains challenging due to limited spectral coverage and a lack of harmonized reflectance products. As an alternative to traditional bio-optical methods, deep learning-based image classification offers a data-driven approach that can overcome many of these limitations. This study presents the first successful implementation of vision transformer-based coastal algal bloom mapping using 30-m Landsat-Sentinel-2 images. A globally distributed bloom patch dataset was generated across bloom-prone coastal hotspots worldwide. Four transformer-based architectures were compared against a standard convolutional baseline for fine-scale bloom detection, and assessed under different optical water types and atmospheric and surface conditions. All deep learning models showed strong capabilities in detecting floating bloom areas, with omission and commission errors of 8-65%. Under cloud and glint stress in a time series, the Swin Transformer outperformed traditional spectral-index approaches, which produced widespread false positives, effectively avoiding cloud- and glint-affected pixels. Comparisons with MODIS-derived products further highlighted the benefits of higher spatial resolution in detecting fragmented and irregularly affected blooms. Our findings support deep learning as a reliable tool for medium-resolution, consistent monitoring of floating algal blooms in dynamic coastal environments.

</details>


### [5] [High-Fidelity 3D Geometric Reconstruction of Pelvic Organs from MRI: A Hybrid Deep Learning and Iterative Optimization Approach](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17836)
*Hui Wang,Xiaowei Li,Chenxin Zhang,Yifan Feng,Jianwei Zuo,Yumeng Tang,Xiuli Sun,Jianliu Wang,Bing Xie,Jiajia Luo*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: A hybrid DL and iterative optimization framework for patient-specific 3D reconstruction of pelvic organs from MRI, achieving higher geometric fidelity and mesh quality than standard DL-based approaches.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: High-fidelity, standardized 3D geometry of pelvic organs is needed for accurate pelvic floor modeling and downstream analysis, but prior work is either segmentation-focused or uses post-processing, leading to labor-intensive workflows and variable quality.

Method: Integrates a geometry-aware multi-level DL architecture with a two-stage amortized optimization training strategy and a holistic synergy mechanism. During training, iterative optimization supervises DL; at inference, DL predicts global organ morphology followed by iterative optimization to refine local surfaces and mesh quality.

Result: Demonstrated superior geometric fidelity versus mainstream DL-based reconstruction models. For bladder, rectum, and uterus: lower Chamfer Distances and higher Dice scores. Maintained computational efficiency and improved overall volumetric mesh quality. At the patient level, higher mean values for the 10 worst elements for minSICN and minSIGE compared with traditional post-processing.

Conclusion: The framework effectively combines deep learning with iterative optimization to produce high-quality, patient-specific pelvic organ geometries, offering improved accuracy and mesh integrity while preserving efficiency; promising for pelvic floor modeling and related analyses.

Abstract: Patient-specific 3D reconstruction of pelvic organ geometry from MRI is important for pelvic floor modeling and downstream patient-specific analysis. However, while previous studies have focused primarily on either image segmentation or downstream use of 3D models, the reconstruction of high-fidelity, high-quality geometries remains labor-intensive and poorly standardized. The study introduced a hybrid deformable shape modeling framework that integrates deep learning prediction with iterative optimization for the reconstruction of the bladder, uterus, and rectum. The framework consists of three core components: a geometry-aware multi-level deep learning architecture that preserves topological consistency of pelvic organs; a two-stage amortized optimization training strategy that balances global shape capture and local surface refinement; and a holistic synergy mechanism--where iterative optimization provides supervision for deep learning during the training phase, and during inference, deep learning rapidly predicts the global organ morphology, followed by iterative optimization to refine local surfaces and mesh quality. This framework demonstrated marked superiority in geometric fidelity than current mainstream deep learning-based organ reconstruction models. For individual anatomical structures, the reconstructed 3D geometries for the bladder, rectum, and uterus achieved significantly lower Chamfer Distance values and higher Dice Similarity Coefficient scores. In addition, while maintaining high computational efficiency, the proposed architecture yielded superior overall volumetric mesh quality. At the patient level, the framework achieved higher mean values for the 10 worst elements for both minSICN and minSIGE compared to traditional geometric post-processing algorithms.

</details>


### [6] [GeoDisaster: Benchmarking Orchestrated Agents for Operational Disaster Geo-Intelligence](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17246)
*Maram Hasan,Aman Verma,Savitra Roy,Hariseetharam Gunduboina,Daksh Jain,Muhammad Haris Khan,Subhasis Chaudhuri,Biplab Banerjee*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: GeoDisaster is an operational geospatial disaster reasoning benchmark with 2,921 verified instances across 43 question types and five task families, introducing an 18-tool multi-agent framework using Role-Contract Expectation Alignment to improve tool use, grounding, and consistency beyond current RS-VLMs.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current RS-VLMs excel at interpretation but lack tool-grounded, evidence-backed, executable geo-intelligence required for operational disaster analysis; there is a need for a benchmark and architecture that evaluate and promote such capabilities.

Method: Construct a dataset of 2,921 verified instances across 43 question types and five task families (deforestation monitoring, multi-hazard analysis, building-damage assessment, flood-safe routing, Sentinel-1 SAR flood monitoring). Each instance integrates heterogeneous EO/GIS evidence (optical and SAR imagery, raster masks, vector geometries, roads, exposure). Ground-truth answers derived from executable geospatial workflows with deterministic checks. Propose an orchestrated multi-agent framework with 18 disaster-oriented tools; agents have specialized roles and coordinate via explicit execution contracts; Role-Contract Expectation Alignment (RCEA) combining failure-aware supervised fine-tuning with contract-grounded reinforcement learning on dense step-level signals.

Result: GeoDisaster challenges existing RS-VLMs and agentic systems; incorporating RCEA improves tool usage, evidence grounding, state consistency, and the quality of generated decisions.

Conclusion: The benchmark and RCEA framework advance operational, evidence-backed geospatial reasoning for disaster analysis, enabling reproducible workflows and closer integration of visual-language models with geospatial tools.

Abstract: Remote-sensing vision-language models (RS-VLMs) have advanced Earth-observation analysis toward visual interpretation and instruction-following, yet fall short of operational geo-intelligence, which demands tool-grounded spatial reasoning and structured, evidence-backed decisions. We introduce GeoDisaster, an operational geospatial disaster reasoning benchmark with 2,921 verified instances across 43 question types and five task families: deforestation monitoring, multi-hazard analysis, building-damage assessment, flood-safe routing, and Sentinel-1 SAR flood monitoring. Instances integrate heterogeneous EO/GIS evidence-optical and SAR imagery, raster masks, vector geometries, road networks, and exposure layers-spanning hazard detection, damage assessment, exposure estimation, and diagnostic report generation. Ground-truth answers are grounded in executable geospatial workflows and deterministic consistency checks, removing the need for language-model annotation. We further propose an orchestrated multi-agent framework with 18 disaster-oriented tools, where role-specialized agents coordinate through explicit execution contracts, aligned via Role-Contract Expectation Alignment (RCEA): failure-aware supervised fine-tuning combined with contract-grounded reinforcement learning over dense step-level signals. Experiments show that GeoDisaster challenges existing RS-VLMs and agentic systems, while RCEA improves tool use, evidence grounding, state consistency, and decision generation.

</details>


### [7] [Pulling The REINS: Training-Free Safety Alignment of Video Diffusion Models via Representation Steering](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17257)
*Rohit Kundu,Arindam Dutta,Sarosij Bose,Athula Balachandran,Amit K. Roy-Chowdhury*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: REINS is a training-free inference-time safety steering method for video diffusion models that injects a single linear direction in transformer hidden states (found via supervised PCA on safety labels) to shift generation from unsafe to safe content; effective across 9 models, multiple scales, and both text-to-video and image-to-video generation with minimal overhead.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Open-weight video diffusion models can generate unsafe content; existing defenses require costly safety fine-tuning or external filters that are easily bypassed, motivating a lightweight, training-free safety mechanism that preserves general capability.

Method: Identify a safety-relevant linear subspace in hidden-state activations of video diffusion transformers via supervised PCA on binary safety labels. At inference, inject this direction into hidden states at an intermediate transformer layer to steer generation from harmful content to semantically related safe alternatives. No weight updates or concept enumeration; negligible computational overhead. Mechanistic analysis shows safety information accumulates with depth, but steering effectiveness peaks at ~50% depth.

Result: Redirection of generation from harmful content to safe alternatives demonstrated across 9 video diffusion models, 1.3B–5B parameter scales, and both text-to-video and image-to-video generation; claims the broadest safety evaluation suite in video generation literature.

Conclusion: Shows a training-free, inference-time safety steering approach is feasible and effective, with a fundamental tradeoff between information availability and downstream propagation across network depth. The method is broadly applicable across models and tasks, but relies on linear separability of safety signals and requires further evaluation for generalization and robustness against adversarial content.

Abstract: Open-weight video diffusion models can generate photorealistic unsafe content, from violence to misinformation, yet existing defenses either require expensive safety fine-tuning that degrades general capability, or apply external filters that are trivially bypassed by adversarial prompts. We present REINS (REpresentation-space INference-time Safety steering), a training-free method that aligns video diffusion models at inference time by steering their internal representations toward safe generation. Our key finding is that safety-relevant structure is linearly encoded in the hidden-state activations of video diffusion transformers, and a single direction, discovered via Supervised PCA on binary safety labels, suffices to separate safe from unsafe generation trajectories. At inference, adding this direction to hidden states at an intermediate transformer layer redirects generation from harmful content to semantically related safe alternatives, with no weight updates, no concept enumeration, and negligible computational overhead. Through mechanistic analysis, we reveal that while safety information accumulates monotonically with transformer depth, steering effectiveness peaks at intermediate layers (~50% depth), exposing a fundamental tradeoff between information availability and downstream propagation capacity. We evaluate REINS across 9 video diffusion models, multiple parameter scales (1.3B-5B), and both text-to-video and image-to-video generation, to our knowledge, the broadest safety evaluation suite in the video generation literature.

</details>


### [8] [Training LLMs with Reinforcement Learning over Digital Twin Representations for Reasoning-Intensive Surgical VideoQA](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17279)
*Yiqing Shen,Han Zhang,Mathias Unberath*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: RL-powered decoupling of perception and reasoning using digital twin representations for surgical VideoQA; hierarchical multi-scale modeling with uncertainty; introduces REAL-Colon-Reason benchmark; achieves state-of-the-art on three benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Fragmented spatio-temporal representations in current methods hinder multi-step reasoning in surgical VideoQA; need a framework that preserves continuous relations and leverages LLMs for reasoning.

Method: Train LLMs via reinforcement learning to operate on digital twin representations derived from surgical foundation models, with hierarchical frame/window/procedure representations and probabilistic uncertainty; reward combining format validation, clinical plausibility, and calibration.

Result: State-of-the-art on REAL-Colon-Reason and two existing benchmarks REAL-Colon-VQA and EndoVis18-VQA.

Conclusion: Decoupling perception and reasoning with digital twins and RL enhances surgical VideoQA capabilities, enabling robust multi-step reasoning with uncertainty estimates; introduces a new benchmark to accelerate progress.

Abstract: Surgical video question answering requires multi-step reasoning across semantic, spatial, and temporal dimensions. Existing methods architecturally compress videos into discrete token representations and couple visual perception with reasoning. This approach fragments continuous spatial-temporal relationships and has been shown to restrict multi-step reasoning capabilities. We introduce a reinforcement learning (RL) framework that trains large language models (LLMs) to decouple perception from reasoning by operating over digital twin representations constructed from surgical foundation models. Additionally, we introduce hierarchical representations across frame, temporal window, and procedure levels with probabilistic uncertainty estimates. Finally, we propose a novel reward that combines format validation with accuracy assessment through clinical plausibility evaluation and uncertainty-aware calibration for training. To demonstrate the capabilities of this approach, we introduce REAL-Colon-Reason, a colonoscopic benchmark with 2000 question-answer pairs across three complexity levels. We achieve state-of-the-art performance on REAL-Colon-Reason and two existing surgical VideoQA benchmarks REAL-Colon-VQA and EndoVis18-VQA.

</details>


### [9] [Pareto LoRA: Mitigating Modality Imbalance in Unified Multimodal Models via Pareto-Optimal Gradient Integration](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17296)
*Xiwen Wei,Mark Nutter,Madhusudhanan Srinivasan,Radu Marculescu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Pareto LoRA balances text and image objectives in LoRA fine-tuning of unified multimodal models, yielding improved image quality with preserved text performance by using Pareto-optimal gradient integration for bi-objective optimization.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To address modality imbalance in multimodal instruction tuning where language gradients dominate training, leading to degraded image generation quality, especially under parameter-efficient fine-tuning like LoRA.

Method: Reformulate multimodal instruction tuning as a bi-objective optimization problem and introduce Pareto LoRA, a gradient integration strategy that achieves Pareto-optimal balance by adjusting gradient direction and magnitude for text and image objectives during fine-tuning.

Result: Pareto LoRA consistently improves multimodal generation balance on the CoMM benchmark with Emu2, delivering up to 44.9% gains in perceptual image quality over vanilla LoRA while maintaining comparable text performance.

Conclusion: Pareto LoRA provides a Pareto-optimal solution to gradient interplay between modalities in LoRA-based fine-tuning of UMMs, leading to balanced multimodal generation without sacrificing text capabilities.

Abstract: Unified multimodal models (UMMs) have recently emerged as a promising paradigm for integrating multimodal understanding and generation within a single autoregressive transformer. However, during multimodal instruction tuning, these models often exhibit pronounced modality imbalance: language gradients dominate optimization, thus leading to lower image generation quality, especially under parameter-efficient fine-tuning such as LoRA. In this work, we systematically analyze modality imbalance in LoRA-based fine-tuning of UMMs for interleaved text-image generation. We show that vision modality performance degrades substantially more than text modality performance when compared to unimodal counterparts, and that modality-specific gradients can differ by orders of magnitude across various tasks and layers. Motivated by this observation, we reformulate the multimodal instruction tuning as a bi-objective optimization problem and propose Pareto LoRA, a Pareto-optimal gradient integration strategy that balances the text and image objectives by modulating the gradient direction and strength. Experiments on the CoMM benchmark with Emu2 demonstrate that Pareto LoRA consistently improves multimodal generation balance, achieving up to 44.9% gains in perceptual image quality over vanilla LoRA while maintaining comparable text performance.

</details>


### [10] [Reasoning Text-to-Video Retrieval for Operating Room Clips via Action-Driven Digital Twins](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17298)
*Yiqing Shen,Hao Ding,Mathias Unberath*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: OR3 introduces Action-Driven Digital Twins (ActDTs) for text-to-video retrieval in operating rooms, enabling implicit-query reasoning via imagination-based retrieval and evidence-grounded refinement; evaluated on MM-OR with robotic knee surgeries, achieving state-of-the-art R@1 and R@5.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current text-to-video retrieval models rely on global embeddings and struggle with implicit, step-wise reasoning required for safety-critical OR events. A representation that supports temporal, action-centric reasoning is needed to distinguish similar-looking clips and retrieve relevant events from implicit queries.

Method: Convert video clips to non-overlapping temporal ActDTs that group subject-action-object triplets; use an LLM to imaginatively generate ActDTs from natural-language queries; perform intra-modal matching with a single encoder trained with ActDT-tailored hard negatives; apply evidence-grounded refinement to adjust imagined ActDTs using discrepancies with top candidates to capture procedure-specific patterns.

Result: On MM-OR (276 implicit queries, 386 clips from robotic knee procedures), OR3 achieves 57.6 R@1 and 77.3 R@5, outperforming the strongest baseline, demonstrating fine-grained discrimination via temporal action reasoning.

Conclusion: ActDT-based, imagination-assisted retrieval with refinement is effective for implicit, temporally structured queries in OR videos and can improve retrieval performance over global-embedding baselines.

Abstract: Text-to-video retrieval in operating rooms (OR) is an enabling technology for OR safety, as it allows stakeholders to retrieve and inspect recordings of specific events. However, because the most safety-critical events may not follow the common structure, to unlock its full potential text-to-video retrieval must be able to handle implicit queries that require reasoning to identify the right video (e.g., the step right before clipping). However, existing methods rely on global embeddings that cannot reason over such queries. We propose OR3, a text-to-video retrieval method that converts clips into action-driven digital twins (ActDTs), grouping concurrent subject-action-object triplets under non-overlapping temporal intervals. Moreover, rather than cross-modal matching through paired encoders, OR3 performs imagination-based retrieval where an LLM generates hypothetical ActDTs from queries. This enables intra-modal matching via a single encoder trained with ActDT-tailored hard negatives. Finally, evidence-grounded refinement revises imagined ActDTs based on discrepancies with top candidates to capture procedure-specific patterns. We construct a benchmark from MM-OR with 276 implicit queries across four reasoning categories over 386 clips from robotic knee procedures. OR3 achieves 57.6 R@1 and 77.3 R@5, outperforming the strongest baseline. These results demonstrate that OR3 enables fine-grained discrimination between visually similar OR video clips through temporal action reasoning.

</details>


### [11] [SierpinskiCam: Camera-Controlled Video Retaking with Sierpinski Triangle Pattern Cues](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17310)
*Suttisak Wizadwongsa,Hyelin Nam,Supasorn Suwajanakorn,Jeong Joon Park*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: SierpinskiCam proposes a robust video retaking method that augments geometry-guided 4D scene representations with Sierpinski dome texture cues and a reference-video conditioning mechanism, enabling reliable appearance grounding and improved controllability under large viewpoint changes.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Video retaking from a monocular source suffers when target camera significantly deviates from the source trajectory; geometry-guided 4D representations provide guidance but fail in newly revealed regions, necessitating more robust and appearance-grounded conditioning.

Method: Extend geometry-based 4D scene guidance with Sierpinski dome texture cues that offer trackable features under large viewpoint changes. Introduce reference-video conditioning by appending source-video tokens to target-token sequences and separating streams with negative RoPE indices, enabling appearance grounding without architectural changes or per-video adaptation.

Result: Extensive experiments show significant gains in camera controllability, geometric consistency, and video quality across diverse and challenging retaking scenarios.

Conclusion: SierpinskiCam effectively addresses the degradation of geometry-guided guidance under large viewpoint changes and demonstrates robust conditioning for appearance grounding, advancing video retaking capabilities.

Abstract: Generating novel renderings of a scene along user-defined camera trajectories from a single monocular video, dubbed video retaking, is a compelling but difficult problem in content creation and visual effects. Existing geometry-guided approaches reconstruct a 4D representation from the source video and render it along the target trajectory to condition video diffusion models. However, this guidance degrades as the target camera departs from the source trajectory, leaving newly revealed regions sparse or entirely missing. We propose SierpinskiCam, which addresses this limitation by augmenting geometry-based guidance with Sierpinski dome texture cues that contains rich trackable features even under large viewpoint changes. We further introduce a reference video conditioning mechanism that appends source-video tokens to the target-token sequence and separates the two streams with negative RoPE indices, enabling appearance grounding without architectural modification or per-video adaptation. Extensive experiments show that SierpinskiCam achieves significant gains in camera controllability, geometric consistency, and video quality across diverse and challenging retaking scenarios. Project page: https://hyelinnam.github.io/SierpinskiCam/.

</details>


### [12] [FATE: Pillar Encoding and Frequency-Aware Training for Event-Based Object Detection](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17334)
*Md Tawheedul Islam Bhuian,Kyoung-Don Kang*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: FATE introduces Pillar Encoding and Frequency-Aware Training to preserve intra-window temporal dynamics in event cameras, enabling high-frequency (up to 200 Hz) object detection with minimal overhead and cross-architecture generalization.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Event streams from bio-inspired cameras are sparse and asynchronous; traditional fixed-subbin discretization loses temporal detail and caps inference to low frequencies, hindering performance on fast dynamics.

Method: Pillar Encoding (PE) assembles events into spatial pillars per macro-accumulation window and projects their intra-window evolution onto a continuous-time orthogonal polynomial basis to obtain an L2-optimal dense pseudo-image. Frequency-Aware Training (FAT) uses a soft mean-teacher curriculum to produce temporally dense pseudo-labels, aligning high-frequency inference with low-frequency supervision.

Result: Experiments show robust generalization across architectures, outperforming strong baselines, enabling object detection at up to 200 Hz with only modest increases in parameters and latency.

Conclusion: FATE provides a compact, generalizable framework that preserves temporal dynamics in event-camera data and bridges supervision-inference frequency gaps, achieving high-temporal-resolution perception with efficient overhead.

Abstract: Event cameras are bio-inspired sensors that asynchronously capture logarithmic intensity changes, offering inherent advantages in high-speed and high-dynamic-range scenarios. However, the sparse and asynchronous nature of event streams poses a fundamental challenge for modern deep learning architectures. To enable compatibility with standard models, most existing approaches partition the accumulation window into fixed temporal sub-bins. While effective for spatial processing, this internal discretization discards fine-grained temporal structure and constrains inference to the low temporal frequencies imposed by training supervision. To address this limitation, we propose FATE, a unified framework built upon a novel Pillar Encoding (PE). While operating over discrete macro-accumulation windows dictated by the target frequency, PE avoids internal temporal sub-binning. It organizes events into spatial pillars and approximates their intra-window evolution via projection onto a continuous-time orthogonal polynomial basis. This formulation yields an L2-optimal representation that retains rich temporal dynamics in a dense pseudo-image, mitigating information loss under sparse event conditions. To fully leverage this representation, we introduce Frequency-Aware Training (FAT), a soft mean-teacher curriculum that generates temporally dense pseudo-labels, effectively bridging the mismatch between low-frequency supervision and high-frequency inference. Extensive experiments demonstrate that FATE generalizes across architectural paradigms and consistently outperforms strong baselines. It enables robust object detection at high temporal resolutions up to 200 Hz, while incurring minimal overhead in parameter count and inference latency

</details>

Here, we develop the first principled method for unsupervised learning of a set of statistics that are used to constrain a maximum entropy probability model. The problem is formulated within a Bayesian framework as a linear inverse problem, with prior distributions assigned to the unknown model parameters. Specifically, the image to be reconstructed is assumed to be sparse in a given basis. We develop a general framework applicable to any basis and as examples, we test the sparsity of the image in its (1) spatial gradients using a total variation prior model, and in its (2) wavelet transform. A Markov chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) method, based on a split-and-augmented Gibbs sampler, is then employed to sample from the posterior distribution of the unknown parameters. The non-differentiable conditional distributions are efficiently sampled using a proximal MCMC method. The proposed algorithms are validated on both single-coil and multi-coil datasets using various k-space sub-sampling patterns and ratios. The results demonstrate the superior performance of each proposed approach in reconstructing images compared to its counterpart optimisation-based method. Moreover, our framework effectively quantifies uncertainty, showing a notable correlation between estimated uncertainty maps and error maps computed using ground truth and reconstructed images, compared with existing deep learning-based methods.

Self-play in vectorized simulators changes the economics: millions of rollout steps per second, and a state distribution naturally rich in collisions, near-misses, and recoveries that no driving log contains. Our approach exploits this asymmetry by decoupling learning to drive from learning to see. We pretrain a single policy by self-play, then align its latent space with a pretrained vision backbone, through the action KL divergence and a batch-relational low-rank structural loss. The action target comes from the self-play policy, so alignment never supervises against a logged trajectory: a paired dataset of (image, scene-state) frames suffices, with no need for the curated expert demonstrations that imitation pretraining is built on. On photorealistic 3D Gaussian splatting closed-loop scenarios, the resulting end-to-end policy matches or exceeds prior end-to-end methods.

### [21] [Visuals Lie, Consistency Speaks: Disentangling Spatial Attention from Reliability in Vision-Language Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17389)
*Logan Mann,Yi Xia,Ajit Saravanan,Ishan Dave,Saadullah Ismail,Shikhar Shiromani,Emily Huang,Ruizhe Li,Kevin Zhu*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Reliability in Vision-Language Models (VLMs) is not anchored to visual grounding; attention maps are poor reliability indicators, while generation dynamics and hidden-state distributions drive truthfulness. Self-Consistency across reasoning paths is the best predictor of correctness; architectural differences cause divergent reliability behavior under interventions.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Challenge the Attention-Confidence Assumption by systematically examining reliability signals across contemporary VLMs, quantify how structural visual attention relates to accuracy, and understand how reliability emerges during generation.

Method: Introduce the VRP (VLM Reliability Probe) across model families. Define structural-attention metrics (cluster counts C_k and spatial entropy H_s) to quantify the visual encoder's gaze and track Delta H_s across layers. Assess correlation with accuracy, perform causal interventions, compare models (LLaVA, PaliGemma, Qwen2-VL), analyze Self-Consistency across reasoning paths, and examine generation-time dynamics and hidden-state distributions as reliability indicators.

Result: Spatial attention shows near-zero correlation with accuracy (R ~ 0.001). Reliability aligns with generation-time dynamics and internal-state distributions. Self-Consistency (agreement rate across sampled reasoning paths) is the dominant predictor of truth (R = 0.429). Architectural interventions reveal divergence: LLaVA bottlenecks late-stage predictions, while PaliGemma and Qwen2-VL distribute reliability globally and resist disruption even when ~50% of the most predictive layer is destroyed.

Conclusion: Current VLM reliability signals are decoupled from visual grounding maps; reliable behavior is determined by internal dynamics and hidden-state processes during generation. Grounding-based expectations (the Attention-Confidence Assumption) are challenged; evaluation and design should prioritize generation-time behavior and state distributions, and consider cross-model architectural differences.

Abstract: Multimodal Foundation Models are increasingly used as reasoning agents, making reliability, knowing when a model may hallucinate, critical. A common intuition, which we call the Attention-Confidence Assumption, holds that reliability follows from "structural" visual perception: tight attention on relevant regions should signal a trustworthy answer, while scattered attention signals confusion. We challenge this through the VLM Reliability Probe (VRP), a systematic cross-family study of reliability signals in contemporary Vision-Language Models (VLMs). We introduce structural-attention metrics, cluster counts (C_k) and spatial entropy (H_s), to quantify the visual encoder's gaze, and track its evolution (Delta H_s) across layers. This reveals a "Symbolic Detachment": models often "Early Lock" visual features only to diffuse attention later, severing early perception from final generation. Contrary to the grounding hypothesis, we find a "Cluster Failure": spatial attention has near-zero correlation (R approx 0.001) with accuracy. Instead, reliability is a phenomenon of generation dynamics and internal-state distributions. Self-Consistency, the agreement rate across sampled reasoning paths, is the dominant predictor of truth (R = 0.429). Scaling causal interventions exposes a sharp architectural divergence: LLaVA locks its prediction in a fragile late-stage bottleneck, whereas PaliGemma and Qwen2-VL distribute reliability globally, staying resilient even when ~50% or more of their most predictive layer is destroyed. For current VLMs, reliability signals are detached from visual grounding maps and are best inferred from generation-time dynamics and hidden-state probes.

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Quantify how vision-language model components (encoder vs decoder) contribute to alignment with human fixation patterns and neural data across tasks, to understand top-down vs bottom-up influences on visual attention.

Method: Comparative analysis of six vision-language models on 200 images across two tasks (general description and social captioning). A 2x2 factorial design of CNN vs ViT encoders crossed with LSTM vs Transformer decoders, plus Molmo 7B-D and Qwen3.5 9B. Measured spatial attention maps against human fixation heatmaps, human noise ceiling, task differentiation, and spatial concentration. Additional experiments: hemispatial negation simulation; TRIBE-simulated synthetic neural responses to assess alignment with synthetic brain activity, focusing on early visual cortex.

Result: Decoder architecture dominated alignment (LSTM vs Transformer yielded 40–50 percentage point gains, 80–87% vs 40–59% of the human noise ceiling). Encoder type contributed a secondary 5–20 point advantage; CNN-LSTM was most aligned (85–87%). LSTM decoders produced diffuse, less task-differentiated maps; ViT-Transformer had the strongest task differentiation and sharp spatial concentration but the weakest alignment. Hemispatial-neglect simulation showed LSTM decoders are more affected by attention ablation than Transformer decoders. In TRIBE-based extension, CNN-Transformer alignment with synthetic neural activity exceeded fixation alignment, best predicting early visual cortex activity. Overall, top-down and bottom-up components trade off predictive alignment across behavioral and synthetic neural data.

Conclusion: Top-down (decoder) and bottom-up (encoder) components jointly shape attention alignment with human data, with decoder choice being the primary driver. The results reveal a trade-off: highly aligned models (esp. with LSTM decoders) can be spatially diffuse and less task-differentiated, while sharper, more differentiated attention (ViT-Transformer) may reduce fixation alignment yet better predict neural signals. This dissociation suggests complementary roles for top-down and bottom-up processes in visual attention, and that model evaluation should consider both behavioral alignment and neural predictivity.

Abstract: Visual perception depends on top-down goals and bottom-up sensory mechanisms. Vision-language models implement both, allowing us to treat each component as a separable hypothesis about what drives where we look. We compared spatial attention maps from six vision-language models against human fixation heatmaps recorded on 200 images during two tasks (general description and social captioning). The six models spanned a 2$\times$2 factorial of CNN vs.\ ViT encoders crossed with LSTM vs.\ Transformer decoders, plus Molmo 7B-D and Qwen3.5 9B. We found that both decoder and encoder architecture shaped alignment, but decoder choice dominated. LSTM vs.\ Transformer decoders increased alignment by 40--50 percentage points (80--87\% vs.\ 40--59\% of the human noise ceiling). In contrast, CNN vs.\ ViT encoders contributed a secondary 5--20 point advantage depending on decoder family, with CNN-LSTM the most aligned model overall (85--87\%). Despite their alignment advantage, LSTM-decoder attention maps were spatially diffuse and minimally task-differentiated; ViT-Transformer, the weakest in alignment, showed the sharpest spatial concentration and strongest task differentiation. A hemispatial-neglect simulation confirmed that ablating attention impacted LSTM decoders more than Transformer decoders. In an exploratory extension using TRIBE-simulated synthetic neural responses, fixation alignment and neural relevance dissociate: CNN-Transformer attention maps better predicted synthetic brain activity despite lower fixation alignment, with attention maps best predicting early visual cortex. Together, top-down and bottom-up components trade off what they predict in behavioral and synthetic neural data.

</details>

This limitation prevents VLMs from capturing essential cross-scale representations and learning evidence-based reasoning. However, creating such a task reveals a critical challenge: multi-image visual question answering (VQA) is prone to text-only shortcuts, which allow models to guess answers using magnification-dependent artifacts rather than visual evidence. To address this, we propose a leakage-aware curation pipeline that combines adversarial text-only screening with constraint-guided question design. Prior memory approaches either update too frequently, retrieve from demonstrations, or only act at sub-goal events without explicit sub-task hand-offs, leading to brittleness on tasks requiring cross-subtask coordination.

Method: Introduce WeaveLA, a cross-subtask memory interface built on a frozen VLA backbone. The core issue is structural: short-window VLAs lack an explicit channel for rouxting information across sub-task boundaries, and existing memory-augmented variants either write at every frame, retrieve from demonstration-time stages, or fire at sub-goal events without performing an explicit sub-task-to-sub-task hand-off into the action expert. We identify the sub-goal completion event as the natural temporal unit for cross-subtask memory hand-off, and present WeaveLA (Weave Latent memory for Vision-Language-Action policies), a cross-subtask memory interface that, on top of a frozen VLA backbone, compresses each completed segment into latent tokens via query-driven attention pooling and routes them directly into the action-generation path of the next sub-task. This event-triggered, action-side design preserves the base policy's short-window interface while adding a lightweight cross-subtask channel. Through stratified evaluation on RoboMME with a $π_{0.5}$ backbone, WeaveLA's gains land exactly where the channel is needed: on the hardest repetition slice (SwingXtimes, $N{=}3$), success rises from $0\%$ to $47.8\%$, while single-execution episodes remain unchanged. ### [34] [StereoFactory: A Unified Merging Framework for Robust Stereo Matching](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17475)
*Xianda Guo,Pinhan Fu,Ruilin Wang,Wenke Huang,Mang Ye,Qin Zou*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: StereoFactory is a two-stage evolutionary framework for post-hoc merging of stereo models, using a genetic algorithm to pick participating models and CMA-ES to route knowledge at the module level, yielding better performance with low retraining time.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To overcome the scalability bottleneck of re-training foundation-model-based stereo matching when incorporating new data; avoid harmful task-vector interference and enable scalable knowledge merging through selective model combination.

Method: Stage 1 uses a genetic algorithm to search the combinatorial space of model subsets and decide which models participate. Stage 2 uses CMA-ES to optimize architecture-adaptive routing across the selected task vectors at the module level (with optional per-module scaling), addressing knowledge specialization across modules.

Result: On two architectures and four benchmarks, StereoFactory achieves the best four-benchmark average under the same checkpoint pool, lowering average error from 3.80 to 3.30 on NMRF and from 2.88 to 2.19 on FoundationStereo relative to the strongest baseline. Post-hoc search requires only 2.7–3.7% of equivalent joint-retraining wall-clock time. Knowledge contributions are module-specific, and selected subsets transfer across architectures with minimal degradation.

Conclusion: Knowledge contributions are inherently module-specific; selective subsets can transfer across architectures with minimal degradation. Code will be released publicly upon acceptance (GitHub link provided in the abstract).

Abstract: Stereo matching has advanced through foundation models trained on large-scale datasets, yet this paradigm suffers from a scalability bottleneck: incorporating new data requires costly joint retraining. Model merging offers a scalable post-hoc alternative by integrating knowledge from specialized models after source checkpoints are available. However, existing merging methods typically retain all available models or rely on greedy inclusion, which can preserve harmful task-vector interference. We propose StereoFactory, a coarse-to-fine evolutionary framework for adaptive model merging. Stage~1 employs a genetic algorithm to search the combinatorial space of model subsets, determining which models should participate. Stage~2 addresses module-level knowledge specialization (different functional modules exhibit distinct preferences for knowledge sources) through CMA-ES optimization of architecture-adaptive routing over the selected task vectors, with optional module-level scaling. Experiments across two architectures and four benchmarks demonstrate that StereoFactory consistently achieves the best four-benchmark average under the same checkpoint pool, reducing the average error from 3.80 to 3.30 on NMRF and from 2.88 to 2.19 on FoundationStereo relative to the strongest controlled baseline. The post-hoc search requires only 2.7--3.7\% of the corresponding joint-retraining wall-clock time. Analysis reveals that knowledge contributions are inherently module-specific, and selected subsets can transfer across architectures with minimal degradation.   <summary>Details</summary>

Across diverse spatial benchmarks, SR-REAL significantly outperforms spatial VLM baselines: (i) a single RL-trained model supports both reasoning paths, with DTR excelling in region-aware tasks through precise 3D localization and LOR enhancing general spatial reasoning; (ii) jointly training both paths fosters mutual reinforcement; (iii) high-quality, blended cold-start data is crucial for stable RL optimization; and (iv) the model generalizes across datasets and domains without per-task tuning, demonstrating positive transfer between LOR and DTR.

Through first-order gradient analysis, we formalize this as gradient incompatibility and theoretically establish the necessity of decoupled optimization. We further reveal that these conflicting threats exhibit separable spectral characteristics in the frequency domain. Motivated by this observation, we propose Threat-aware Frequency Decoupling (TaFD), a two-stage defense framework that reformulates JAT as a frequency-domain divide-and-conquer paradigm. TaFD first discovers latent threat domains via unsupervised clustering of attack spectral prototypes and trains a lightweight classifier for inference-time threat domain identification. Conditioned on the prediction, TaFD employs a Frequency-Conditional Convolution that learns threat-domain-specific spectral masks and routes each sample to the corresponding expert, enforcing structural parameter separation and alleviating optimization conflicts.
  We validate TaFD on three representative image-classification benchmarks (CIFAR-10, CIFAR-100, and Tiny-ImageNet) and on two representative architectures (the convolutional ResNet and the hybrid-transformer MobileViT). Extensive results demonstrate that TaFD achieves more balanced robustness against heterogeneous attacks than existing JAT and frequency-domain baselines, improving average robust accuracy by approximately 11\% over the strongest baseline while maintaining leading clean accuracy.

### [45] [TivTok: Broadcasting Time-Invariant Tokens for Scalable Video Tokenization](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17590)
*Weiliang Chen,Yuanhui Huang,Xuebo Wang,Yueqi Duan*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: TivTok introduces a time-invariant and time-variant token decomposition for video tokens, enabling reuse of persistent information across frames via Scope-Induced Factorization (SIF) and Invariant Broadcasting (IB), achieving significant token efficiency and compression gains on standard benchmarks.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Improve scalability of video generation by reducing token redundancy across time; existing tokenizers compress but still redundantly encode static content (backgrounds, object appearance) across frames.

Method: Decompose a video clip into Time-Invariant (TIV) tokens carrying shared information and Time-Variant (TV) tokens carrying frame-specific residuals. Use Scope-Induced Factorization to give TIV full-clip attention and TV attention limited to their frame plus TIV. Decoder employs Invariant Broadcasting to reuse TIV across frames/chunks for parallel reconstruction.

Result: Empirical results show rFVD = 12.65 on 16×256×256; 2.91× compression efficiency gain on 128-frame videos vs baselines; uses 1.1% of tokens compared with downsample-based tokenizers.

Conclusion: Factorizing tokens into reusable Time-Invariant components and frame-specific residuals with SIF and IB yields substantial token efficiency and compression gains for scalable video generation without sacrificing reconstruction quality.

Abstract: Video tokenization is fundamental to scalable video generation, as the number of tokens directly determines the computational cost and the length of videos that can be modeled. Existing tokenizers mainly improve scalability by compressing videos into fewer tokens, but they often continue to represent persistent content, such as static backgrounds and consistent object appearances, repeatedly across frames and chunks. In this paper, we propose \textbf{TivTok} (\textit{Time-Invariant Tokenizer}), a reuse-aware video tokenizer that makes persistent information reusable across time. TivTok represents a clip with Time-Invariant (TIV) tokens that encode information shared across frames and Time-Variant (TV) tokens that encode frame-specific residuals. To obtain this factorization, we introduce Scope-Induced Factorization (SIF), which assigns different attention scopes to the two token groups: TIV tokens attend to the full clip, whereas each TV token only accesses its corresponding frame together with the TIV tokens. In the decoder, Invariant Broadcasting (IB) reuses the same TIV tokens across frames and chunks for parallel reconstruction and long-video tokenization. Experiments show that TivTok achieves an rFVD of 12.65 on the standard $16{\times}256{\times}256$ benchmark and improves compression efficiency by 2.91$\times$ for 128-frame videos compared with the evaluated baselines, while using only 1.1\% of the tokens required by downsample-based tokenizers in our evaluation.

TL;DR: A Robust-TOOC benchmark for text-guided open-vocabulary object counting under six corruptions, and Dual-TTT, a test-time training framework that freezes the counting model and learns a TL-Denoiser to denoise image representations, enabling annotated-free robustness improvements across existing TOOC baselines.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: TOOC methods excel on ideal images but fail under real-world degradations. A dedicated benchmark and a lightweight, annotation-free robustness method are needed to evaluate and improve TOOC performance in adverse conditions.

Method: Introduce Dual-TTT, which at test time updates only a Text-guided Lightweight Denoiser (TL-Denoiser) to remove corruption-aware noise from image representations, while keeping the original counting network frozen. TL-Denoiser is diffusion-inspired and trained at test time in an annotation-free manner, enabling integration with existing TOOC models without architectural changes.

Result: Extensive experiments show that Dual-TTT improves robustness of multiple recent TOOC baselines across six corruption types (rain, fog, darkness, Gaussian noise, salt-and-pepper noise, and mixed corruption) without requiring extra annotations.

Conclusion: Robust-TOOC provides a practical benchmark for evaluating TOOC under real-world corruptions and a lightweight, annotation-free test-time strategy (Dual-TTT) to enhance robustness with minimal modification to existing TOOC systems.

Abstract: Text-guided Open-vocabulary Object Counting (TOOC) enables counting arbitrary object categories specified by text prompts, offering substantially greater flexibility than conventional closed-set counting. However, existing TOOC methods are developed and evaluated primarily on ideal images, while real-world scenes often suffer from adverse conditions such as rain, fog, darkness, and sensor noise, which severely degrade visual quality and impair vision-language alignment. To bridge this gap, we introduce Robust-TOOC, the first benchmark for evaluating TOOC under diverse corruption conditions, which covers six representative degradation types: rain, fog, darkness, Gaussian noise, salt-and-pepper noise, and mixed corruption. To improve robustness while preserving the original counting architecture, we propose Dual-TTT, a dual-architecture test-time training framework for TOOC. Specifically, during test-time training, Dual-TTT updates only the Text-guided Lightweight Denoising module (TL-Denoiser), while keeping the original counting network frozen. Inspired by diffusion models, the TL-Denoiser is optimized to remove corruption-aware noise from image representations under degraded conditions. Since only the TL-Denoiser is trained at test time, Dual-TTT is annotation-free and can be seamlessly integrated into existing TOOC models without modifying their original architecture. Extensive experiments on multiple recent TOOC baselines demonstrate the effectiveness of our method.

MoVP is composed of four stages: (i) a Mixture-of-View soft router with twelve expert MLPs that learns view-dependent expert preferences without camera-identity supervision; (ii) cross-view attention to align synchronized cameras; (iii) learnable prototype anchoring to condition the representation on class-level reference vectors; and (iv) a prototype-conditioned gated projection that produces the final skill embedding. In Ego+Exos, SkillMoV remains close to the best reported result in that setting (47.63% versus 48.20%). Ablations on the selected Exos configuration validate each component: MoV routing contributes +6.61 pp over attentive aggregation, cross-view attention +4.92 pp, prototype anchoring +4.07 pp, and stochastic view dropout +3.90 pp. Through LoRA adaptation, SkillMoV trains only 23.32% of its parameters and adds limited measured overhead relative to a LoRA-only baseline.

Method: A fully-local pipeline: an orchestrator chunks video and outputs top-k candidate labels per segment; an ensemble of heterogeneous VLM specialists (from different model families) engages in structured deliberation including peer-question rounds; agent rankings are combined via a Borda count, and the orchestrator re-ranks its own predictions in light of the specialists' evidence; no fine-tuning performed.

We propose Divide, Deliberate, Decide, a fully-local, zero-shot multi-agent framework in which (i) a VLM orchestrator chunks the video and proposes a top-k candidate label list per segment, (ii) an ensemble of heterogeneous VLM specialists, drawn from different open model families, engages in a structured deliberation that includes a peer-consultation round of questions, and (iii) agent rankings are aggregated with a Borda count and the orchestrator re-ranks its own prediction in light of the specialists' evidence. The entire pipeline runs locally with no fine-tuning. Experiments show that our method positively improves zero-shot action recognition performance over the baseline, highlighting the influence of a heterogeneous deliberation step, showing that the gain stems from decorrelated model priors rather than from additional compute.

To address these challenges, we present MOCHI (MOtion Enhancement of Collaborative Human-object Interactions), a two-stage framework for enhancing noisy MHOI data. Our approach first generates physically plausible hand grasps through optimization from noisy body input, producing grasps that are both physically plausible and semantically consistent with the body pose, where these optimized grasps are extended into complete hand-object interaction sequences. Consequently, the full-body motion for all participants are refined through a diffusion-based noise optimization framework that uses single-person motion priors. Outputs per patch include 20+ compositional/morphological/spatial metrics; encoded as JSON and fed to a fine-tuned NVIDIA BioNeMo GPT to generate clinical narratives. Result: Feasibility and internal consistency demonstrated; the approach yields rich TME feature representations and interpretable narratives, with publicly released data and model checkpoints to support large-scale TME profiling.

Conclusion: The framework is feasible for large-scale TME profiling from routine histology, enabling interpretable clinical narratives and providing resources to the community for spatial biology research; limitations likely include dependence on pseudo-label quality and need for external clinical outcome validation.

Abstract: Characterising the tumour microenvironment (TME) from routine H&E-stained histology images requires simultaneous cell segmentation, feature extraction, and interpretable clinical reporting. We present SEGTME-UNI2, a unified framework addressing these requirements. Its core is UNI2-UPERHOVER, a dual-head segmentation model pairing the UNI2-H pathology foundation model (ViT-Giant, pretrained on >100M tiles from 100K slides) with two parallel UperNet decoders: one for six-class semantic segmentation and one for horizontal-vertical gradient regression enabling watershed-based nuclear instance separation. To address the lack of pixel-level annotations in large real-world repositories, UNI2-UPERHOVER undergoes a three-stage progressive pseudo-label curriculum. Each stage trains a fresh model without weight transfer, driving improvement entirely via increased pseudo-label quality: Stage 1: Uses human-annotated PanNuke (7,901 images, 189,744 nuclei, 0.25 um/pixel). Stage 2: Uses entropy-filtered pseudo-labels from the Stage 1 model on 271,711 TCGA-UT scale-0 patches (0.5 um/pixel). Stage 3: Uses pseudo-labels from the Stage 2 model on all 1,608,060 TCGA-UT patches across six resolution scales (0.5-1.0 um/pixel). Segmentation outputs feed a structured TME feature extraction pipeline computing 20+ per-patch compositional, morphological, spatial entropy, and intercellular distance metrics. These are encoded as JSON and passed to a fine-tuned NVIDIA BioNeMo GPT model to generate clinically interpretable TME narratives. Preliminary validation on held-out PanNuke and TCGA-UT partitions demonstrates framework feasibility and internal consistency. The pseudo-labelled TCGA-UT dataset and UNI2-UPERHOVER checkpoint are publicly released to support large-scale TME profiling and spatial biology research.

</details>


### [58] [Vision-language models for chest radiography do not always need the image](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17710)
*Mahshad Lotfinia,Sebastian Ziegelmayer,Lisa Adams,Daniel Truhn,Andreas Maier,Soroosh Tayebi Arasteh*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Causal auditing shows chest radiograph vision-language models may rely on priors rather than actual images; text-only models can match multimodal performance, questioning the interpretation of accuracy as image-grounded evidence.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To determine whether medical vision-language models truly use image data or rely on prior information, and to establish robust evaluation that separates image-guided reasoning from priors.

Method: A causal audit intervenes on the input image: occluding the relevant region, occluding an irrelevant region, and swapping in another patient's same-label scan. It combines three behavioral metrics to assess dependency on the image. Evaluated across nine models, two datasets, and varying prompts, then categorized models into groups based on image use.

Result: Text-only models approach within 5.7 accuracy points of the best multimodal model; a 119B multimodal model is statistically indistinguishable from a 7B text-only baseline. The audit identifies models that ignore the image, are unstable, or use the image selectively across findings; results hold across datasets, resolution, and prompts. Compared with radiologists, a text-only model matches accuracy with zero grounding, while image-using models achieve radiologist-like grounding. Confidence signals only reflect image use. Grounding, not accuracy, should govern clinical deployment.

Conclusion: Grounding audits are essential to validate true image utilization and should gate clinical deployment of medical VLMs; relying solely on accuracy may overstate the model's reliance on image data.

Abstract: Medical vision-language models report strong chest radiograph accuracy, and this is increasingly read as evidence that they use the image. That inference is unsafe: a model exploiting finding-name priors scores like one that reads the scan, and no standard benchmark separates them. We introduce a causal audit that intervenes on the image, occluding the relevant region, occluding an irrelevant one, and swapping in another patient's same-label scan, and combines three behavioral metrics to test whether a correct answer depends on the image. Across nine systems, a text-only model with no image access reaches within 5.7 accuracy points of the best multimodal one, and a 119-billion-parameter multimodal model is statistically indistinguishable from a 7-billion text-only baseline. The audit splits the cohort into three models that ignore the image, one that is unstable, and five that use it selectively, for a subset of findings; the categories hold across a second dataset, resolution, and prompt phrasing. Against board-certified radiologists, a text-only model is statistically indistinguishable from a radiologist's accuracy while grounding at zero, whereas the image-using models ground at radiologist-comparable rates. Reported confidence flags ungrounded answers only when a model uses the image. Grounding audits, not accuracy, should gate clinical deployment.

### [59] [Structured Adversarial Camouflage via Voronoi Diagrams](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17711)
*Jens Bayer,Stefan Becker,David Münch,Michael Arens,Jürgen Beyerer*

Main category: cs.CV

TL;DR: Adversarial Voronoi camouflage optimizes seed-point locations under fixed color palettes to create structured, camouflaged patterns. It is parameter-efficient, improves visual plausibility, transfers across detectors and backgrounds, but degrades detector performance. Repainting palettes largely nullifies the effect; physical validation and color calibration remain for future work.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Reduce the computational burden and visual detectability of pixel-wise adversarial patches by proposing a palette-constrained, seed-point–based approach that yields plausible camouflage while remaining attack-viable in security-critical settings.

Method: Voronoi tessellation with seed-point optimization and soft color assignment to a fixed palette; no additional regularization. Compare naive Inria->COCO placement vs proposed method; also apply garment-level segmentation masks (3DPeople). Assess transfer across detectors (YOLOv9–YOLOv12), robustness to background shifts, and effect of palette changes and color tweaks.

Result: The naive placement performs poorly (baseline). The proposed method yields comparable or better attack impact on COCO-style AP@[.5:.95] in general but shows a significant drop for garment-level segmentation. The attack transfers across background domains and detector families, indicating black-box robustness. Palette repainting largely neutralizes the effect; single-color tweaks show low tolerance (≤0.17). The design achieves parameter efficiency and plausibility at the cost of detector performance; physical validation and color calibration are left for future work.

Conclusion: Palette-constrained seed-point optimization via Voronoi tessellation provides a space-efficient, visually plausible adversarial camouflage with cross-domain transferability and detector-family robustness, but requires validation in real-world settings and calibration of colors for reliable results.

Abstract: Pixel-wise adversarial patches are computationally heavy and often visually detectable, limiting utility in security-critical systems. We present adversarial Voronoi camouflage that optimizes only seed-point locations under fixed, printable palettes using a soft assignment, producing structured, splinter camouflage-like patterns without additional regularization. Evaluated on person detection with COCO-style AP@[.5:.95], naive placement (Inria -> COCO) performs comparably bad, while garment-level application via segmentation mask (3DPeople) results in a significant AP drop. The attack transfers to out-of-domain backgrounds and across detector families (YOLOv9/10/11/12), indicating robustness in black-box settings. Repainting with different palettes largely nullifies the effect, and single-color tweaks show limited tolerance (<=0.17), highlighting a structure-palette coupling. The parameter-efficient, palette-constrained design improves visual plausibility while degrading real-time detector performance. Physical validation and color calibration are left for future work.
  Code: https://github.com/JensBayer/Voronoi

Comparisons with existing global LULC products and analyses under different cloud-cover levels further demonstrate the robustness and practical value of CloudLULC-Net for target-date LULC mapping in cloud-prone regions.The project is publicly available at: https://github.com/RSIIPAC/CloudLULC

### [61] [GSPan: A Continuous Gaussian Primitive Representation for Arbitrary-Scale Pansharpening](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.17722)
*Fangyi Li,Xiaoyuan Yang,Yixiao Li,Zongyang Sui,Kangqing Shen,Gemine Vivone*

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Fixed-grid pansharpening limits scale adaptation and generalization to arbitrary target grids; a continuous Gaussian representation could enable flexible, scale-decoupled fusion.

Method: A Dual-Stream Hierarchical Interaction (DSHI) with a Spatial-Spectral Interactive Attention (SSIA) estimates band-wise Gaussian primitives from complementary PAN and MS inputs. These primitives render a residual detail field that is injected into the upsampled MS image. A Scale-Decoupled Asymmetric Inference (SDAI) strategy estimates primitives at reduced resolution and renders the fused image at the target resolution.

Conclusion: Continuous Gaussian residual representations offer a flexible, scale-decoupled alternative to fixed-grid predictions for pansharpening, enabling arbitrary-resolution rendering and efficient inference.

Most existing deep learning methods treat pansharpening as fixed-grid prediction, which limits scale adaptation. To address this, we propose GSPan, a framework that introduces 2D Gaussian Splatting (GS) into pansharpening. Instead of directly predicting pixels, GSPan represents band-wise residual details as continuous and learnable 2D Gaussian primitives. We design a Dual-Stream Hierarchical Interaction (DSHI) architecture with a Spatial-Spectral Interactive Attention (SSIA) module to estimate these primitives from complementary PAN and MS observations. The predicted primitives are rendered as a residual detail field and injected into the upsampled MS image. This continuous representation allows GSPan to render fused images on arbitrary target sampling grids without scale-specific retraining. It further enables a Scale-Decoupled Asymmetric Inference (SDAI) strategy, which estimates primitives at a reduced resolution and renders the fused image at the target resolution for efficient large-scene pansharpening. Experiments on QuickBird, GaoFen-2, WorldView-3, and WorldView-3-4K datasets show that GSPan delivers state-of-the-art fusion performance. Moreover, SDAI markedly accelerates inference, achieving a favorable trade-off between computational efficiency and fusion quality. Our results demonstrate the potential of continuous Gaussian residual representations as a flexible and scale-decoupled alternative to fixed-grid prediction.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Bridge the navigation-centric limitation of current world models by enabling real-time object interactions; tackle data scarcity for human-object interactions and memory inefficiency that erases causal event transitions.

Method: Propose hierarchical action-aware memory that prioritizes interaction relevance, plus a persistent memory bank for long-range event-update and object-identity tokens; build a 100k-interaction video dataset with per-chunk captions via chain-of-thought; integrate into a chunk-autoregressive framework enabling mid-rollout object actions.
